February 3, 2016
Section 18. Investment of Funds and
Subfunds.
(a) Moneys held in the Debt Service
Reserve Fund or in any special
reserve account established pursuant
to Section 5(f) hereof shall be invested and reinvested, in accordance with
written instructions received from
the City, by the Trustee, to the fullest
extent practicable, in Eligible Investments maturing not later than the
final maturity of the Series of Bonds
for which the applicable subaccount
was established or subject to withdrawal at any time required for purposes of the Debt Service Reserve
Fund.
(b) Moneys held in the Debt Service
Fund shall be invested and reinvested, in accordance with written
instructions from the City, by the
Trustee, to the fullest extent possible,
in Eligible Investments maturing
within one (1) year from the date of
purchase but in any event not later
than such times as shall be necessary
to provide moneys for payments to be
made from such Funds as required
herein or subject to withdrawal at
any such time.
(c) Except as otherwise provided in
this General Bond Ordinance with
respect to the investment of moneys
in the Debt Service Fund and the Debt
Service Reserve Fund or any special
reserve account established pursuant
to Section 5(f) hereof, and only to the
extent otherwise provided, moneys
held in the Funds and Subfunds shall
be invested and reinvested by the City
and the Trustee, as the case may be,
to the fullest extent practicable, in
Eligible Investments that mature or
are subject to withdrawal not later
than such times as shall be necessary
to provide moneys for payments to be
made from such Funds and Subfunds,
as required herein and in the applicable Supplemental Bond Ordinance or
Supplemental Trust Agreement; provided, however, that the Trustee shall
make such investments only in accordance with instructions received from
the City.
(d) An investment that can be
redeemed at the option of the holder
or that may be sold at a pre-established price to a “Qualified Purchase
Agreement Provider” (as hereinafter
defined) pursuant to a written agreement within a specified time period
shall be deemed to mature within that
specified time period for purposes of
limitations in this General Bond Ordinance on the maximum maturity of
investments, but only for as long as
the redemption or sale option remains
exercisable within the specified period. For purposes of this Section 18(d),
a “Qualified Purchase Agreement
Provider” means a financial institution, including, without limitation, a
bank (including the Trustee or any of
its affiliates) or insurance company)
that is rated, or the obligations of
which are rated, in one of the top two
rating categories by at least two Rating Agencies.
Section 19. Valuation and Sale of
Investments.
(a) In computing the amount in any
Fund or Subfund established under
the provisions of this General Bond
Ordinance, obligations purchased as
an investment of moneys therein
shall be valued at the lower of market
value or the amortized value thereof.
Amortized value, when used with
respect to an obligation purchased at
par, means the par amount thereof,
and, when used with respect to an

February 3, 2016
obligation purchased at a premium
above or a discount below par, means
the value as of any given time
obtained by dividing the total premium or discount at which such obligation was purchased by the number of
interest payments remaining on such
obligation after such purchase and
deducting the amount thus calculated
for each interest payment date after
such purchase from the purchase
price in the case of an obligation purchased at a premium and adding the
amount thus calculated for each interest payment date after such purchase
to the purchase price in the case of an
obligation purchased at a discount.
(b) Except as otherwise provided
herein, the Trustee shall sell at the
best price obtainable, using reasonable diligence to determine such best
price, or present for redemption, any
obligation so purchased as an investment whenever it shall be so requested in writing by the Director of
Finance or whenever it shall be necessary in order to provide moneys to
meet any payment or transfer from
any Fund held by it.
(c) Investments purchased as an
investment of moneys in any Fund or
Subfund shall be deemed at all times
to be a part of such Fund or Subfund,
and any losses suffered due to the
investment thereof shall be charged
to such Fund or Subfund. A deficiency
in a Subfund in the Debt Service
Reserve Fund shall not be deemed to
exist as of a date of transfer for the
purposes of this subsection (c) if the
amount on deposit therein is less than
the applicable Debt Service Reserve
Requirement with respect to any
Series of Bonds solely because as of
such date of transfer one or more
deposits to such Subfund in the Debt
Service Reserve Fund is not required
in connection with the original
issuance of such Series until a future
date or dates.
(d) The valuation and sale of
investments as provided in this Section 19 may be amended in the Master
Trust Agreement or any Supplemental Trust Agreement upon the request
of a Credit Provider.
Section 20. Covenants of the City.
The City hereby covenants with the
Holders of the Bonds as follows:
(a) The City shall maintain the System, or shall cause the System to be
maintained, in sound operating condition and free from any liens or encumbrances that would interfere with the
full and continuous use and operation
thereof by the City.
(b) The City shall keep proper
books of record and account so as to
show the complete financial results of
the operation of the System, including
Revenues and Operating Expenses
and all capital expenditures therefor,
and shall invest and deposit cash
receipts that constitute Revenues in
accordance with applicable laws, this
General Bond Ordinance and the
Trust Agreement.
(c) The City shall at all times prescribe, charge and collect such rates,
rentals and other charges for the use
of the services of the System and shall
restrict the Operating Expenses of
the System in such a way that Net
Revenues Available for Debt Service
(adjusted for purposes of clause (i)
as described in the following sentence) in each Fiscal Year shall be
not less than the greater of (i) 120%
of Debt Service on all Bonds then Outstanding payable during that Fiscal
Year or (ii) 100% of the sum of: (A)

The City Record
Debt Service on all Bonds then Outstanding payable during that Fiscal
Year, (B) all required deposits to the
Debt Service Reserve Fund during
that Fiscal Year, (C) all required
deposits to the Subordinated Debt Service Fund and to any reserve fund
securing Subordinated Indebtedness
during that Fiscal Year, (D) all
required deposits to the Contingency
Fund during that Fiscal Year, and
(E) debt service payable on any other
obligations payable from the Balance
Subfund and deposits to any reserve
funds securing such other obligations
during that Fiscal Year. For purposes
of clause (i) of the preceding sentence, but not for the purpose of
clause (ii) of the preceding sentence,
“Net Revenues Available for Debt Service” for any Fiscal Year shall
include any amounts transferred
from the Rate Stabilization Fund to
the Revenue Fund during such Fiscal
Year, but shall be reduced by any
amounts transferred from the Revenue Fund to the Rate Stabilization
Fund during that period. For purposes of determining the City’s compliance with the rate covenant contained
in this Section 20(d), the amount of
any Direct Payments received by the
City or the Trustee in any Fiscal Year
shall be credited against (i) Debt Service in such Fiscal Year if such Direct
Payment related to Bonds or (ii) debt
service on Subordinated Indebtedness
in such Fiscal Year if such Direct
Payment related to Subordinated
Indebtedness.
(d) If in any Fiscal Year the Net
Revenues Available for Debt Service
shall be less than the amount
required under subsection (c) of this
Section, the City shall, within thirty
(30) days following receipt by the
City of its audited annual financial
statement and the written request of
the Trustee, employ a Consulting
Engineer to make recommendations
within forty-five (45) days as to a
revision of the rates, fees and charges
or Operating Expenses or methods of
operation of the System, if any, that
will result in producing the amount so
required in the next succeeding Fiscal Year. The City covenants and
agrees, promptly upon its receipt of
such recommendations, to revise the
rates, fees, and charges or Operating
Expenses or methods of operation of
the System and to take such other
action as shall be in conformity with
such recommendations to the extent
the City feasibly may do so and to
notify the Trustee of the actions it
has taken. Upon the taking by the
City of such actions, its failure to comply with subsection (c) of this Section
shall not constitute an Event of
Default.
(e) The City shall permit the authorized representative of the Trustee, or
of any Holder or Holders of twentyfive per centum (25%) of the aggregate principal amount of the Bonds at
the time Outstanding, to inspect the
System and all records, accounts, and
data relating to Revenues and the collection thereof, at all reasonable
times.
(f) The City shall not create nor
suffer to be created any pledge, lien,
or charge, except to secure Additional
Bonds issued in accordance herewith,
that would constitute a pledge or lien
prior to, or on a parity with, the
pledge of and lien on Net Revenues
created by this General Bond Ordinance and the Trust Agreement to
secure the Bonds.

167

57
(g) The City shall maintain a risk
management program that provides
protection against risks of damage or
destruction of the System and liabilities for the operations of the System.
In furtherance thereof, the City may,
among other things: self-insure in
whole or in part; adopt alternative or
supplemental risk management programs that the Council of the City
determines to be reasonable; organize
either solely or in connection with
other political subdivisions, organizations or captive insurance companies;
participate in programs of captive
insurance companies organized by
others; establish a self insurance
trust fund; participate in mutual or
other cooperative insurance or other
risk management programs or pools
with other political subdivisions or
organizations; participate in or enter
into agreements with local, State or
federal governments in order to
achieve such insurance; or participate
in other alternative risk management
programs. In case of any damage to or
destruction of any part of the System
amounting to a loss of $500,000 or
more, the City promptly shall give or
cause to be given written notice thereof to the Trustee generally describing
the nature and extent of such damage
or destruction. Regardless of whether
the net proceeds of insurance, if any,
received on account of such damage
or destruction shall be sufficient for
such purpose, the City promptly shall
commence and complete, or cause to
be commenced and completed, the
repair or restoration of the System as
nearly as practicable to the value,
condition and character thereof existing immediately prior to such damage
or destruction, with such changes or
alterations, however, as the City may
deem necessary for proper operation
of the System and as shall not impair
or diminish, in the judgment of the
City, the suitability of the System as a
water pollution control system.
(h) The City shall, for so long as
any Bonds are Outstanding, retain
under the control of the City all facilities from time to time comprising the
System, subject to disposition in the
ordinary course for substitution or
removal upon obsolescence, and will,
in the exercise of such control, comply
with all applicable requirements of
law. For purposes of this covenant,
the term “control” shall include either
the ownership or the operation of
such facilities by the City.
(i) The City shall observe and perform all its agreements and obligations provided for by the Series 2016
Bonds, any Additional Bonds, this
General Bond Ordinance or the Trust
Agreement.
(j) The City shall, for each Fiscal
Year, prepare and adopt, within the
time period and in a manner prescribed by law, a detailed budget of
the estimated Revenues and Operating Expenses of the System. The budget shall provide for all operating
Revenues, including interest income,
and all Operating Expenses and other
commitments required under the
Trust Agreement.
(k) The City shall take whatever
action may be reasonably required to
enforce its rights against any Person
collecting charges on behalf of the
City for the use of the System and to
protect the City’s interest in any
funds collected by such Person that
are payable to the City.
All of the obligations under this
Section 20 are hereby established as

58
duties specifically enjoined by law
and resulting from an office, trust or
station upon the City and its officials
within the meaning of Section 2731.01
of the Ohio Revised Code.
Section 21. Financial Advisors and
Consultants. The Director of Finance
may obtain the services of one or
more Financial Advisors, from time to
time, to assist the Director of Finance
in making any of the determinations
required by this General Bond Ordinance to be determined by the Director of Finance or to negotiate any
Hedge Agreements. The Director of
Finance may rely on the written
advice of any Financial Advisor so
retained. The Director of Finance
may obtain the services of one or
more feasibility consultants, from
time to time, to provide reports in connection with the issuance and sale of
any Bonds or the delivery of any
Hedge Agreements concerning the
utilization and operation of the System, debt service coverage, rates and
charges or other matters. Any Financial Advisor or consultant employed
under the authority of this General
Bond Ordinance shall be disinterested
in the transaction and be independent
of the underwriters or counterparties
and any other party interested in the
transaction.
Section 22. Captions, Headings, and
Section References. The captions and
headings in this General Bond Ordinance are solely for convenience of
reference and in no way define, limit,
or describe the scope or intent of any
Sections, subsections, paragraphs,
subparagraphs, or clauses hereof.
Reference to a Section means a section of this General Bond Ordinance
unless otherwise indicated.
Section 23. Severability. Each section of this General Bond Ordinance
and each subdivision or paragraph of
any section is hereby declared to be
independent and the finding or holding of any section or any subdivision
or paragraph of any section to be
invalid or void shall not be deemed or
held to affect the validity of any other
section, subdivision or paragraph of
this General Bond Ordinance.
Section 24. Interpretation. Any provisions of the Codified Ordinances of
the City which are inconsistent with
the provisions of this General Bond
Ordinance shall not apply to the
Bonds or matters authorized herein.
Nothing in this General Bond Ordinance is intended to, and no provision
hereof shall be applied in any manner
as would, impair the obligation of
contract of the City with respect to
any outstanding bonds, certificates of
indebtedness,
other
obligations,
indentures or other agreements or
contracts made or entered into by the
City.
Section 25. Validity. This Council
finds and determines that this General Bond Ordinance was passed in compliance with all applicable provisions
of the City’s Charter and the rules of
this Council.
Section 26. Compliance with Open
Meeting Requirements. This Council
finds and determines that all formal
actions of this Council and any of its
committees concerning and relating
to the passage of this General Bond
Ordinance were taken in an open
meeting of this Council or committees, and that all deliberations of this
Council and any of its committees
that resulted in those formal actions
were in meetings open to the public,
all in compliance with the law.

The City Record
Section 27. Emergency. This General Bond Ordinance is hereby declared
to be an emergency measure and, provided it receives the affirmative vote
of two-thirds of all members elected
to Council, it shall take effect and be
in force immediately upon its passage
and approval by the Mayor; otherwise
it shall take effect and be in force
from and after the earliest period
allowed by law.
Passed January 25, 2016.
Effective January 26, 2016.

Ord. No. 91-16.
By Council Member Cimperman.
An emergency ordinance consenting and approving the issuance of a
permit for the 14th Annual Walk,
Rock & Run on April 30, 2016, sponsored by the Diversity Center of
Northeast Ohio.
Whereas, this ordinance constitutes
an emergency measure providing for
the usual daily operation of a municipal department; now, therefore
Be it ordained by the Council of the
City of Cleveland:
Section 1. That pursuant to Section
411.06 of the Codified Ordinances of
Cleveland, Ohio 1976, this Council consents to and approves the holding of
the Consenting and approving the
issuance of a permit for the 14th
Annual Walk, Rock & Run on April
30, 2016, sponsored by the Diversity
Center of Northeast Ohio. Start:
Erieside Avenue at the Rock and Roll
Hall of Fame and Museum; Erieside
east to Burke Airport loop; go around
Burke Airport Loop to North Marginal
Road; North Marginal Road west to
East 9th Street; East 9th south to
Lakeside Avenue; Lakeside west to
West 3rd Street; West 3rd south to St.
Clair Avenue; St. Clair west to West
9th; West 9th north to West Lakeside
Avenue (under the Main Avenue
bridge); West Lakeside east to West
3rd; West 3rd north to Erieside
Avenue; Erieside east to Rock and
Roll Hall of Fame and Museum and
Finish; provided that the applicant
sponsor shall meet all the requirements of Section 411.05 of the Codified
Ordinances of Cleveland, Ohio, 1976.
Streets may be closed as determined
by the Chief of Police and safety
forces as may be necessary in order to
protect the participants in the event.
Said permit shall further provide that
the City of Cleveland shall be fully
indemnified from any and all liability
resulting from the issuance of the
same, to the extent and in form satisfactory to the Director of Law.
Section 2. That this ordinance is
hereby declared to be an emergency
measure and, provided it receives the
affirmative vote of two-thirds of all
the members elected to Council, it
shall take effect and be in force immediately upon its passage and approval
by the Mayor; otherwise, it shall take
effect and be in force from and after
the earliest period allowed by law.
Passed January 25, 2016.
Effective January 26, 2016.
